Here are list of tasks that are marked not complete or partially complete.
The task is to go through each line, line by line.
For each line,
1. Check if it is a 'Main task' or a'Sub-task'/component
2. If it is a sub-task/component,
	a. Verify that it is fully implemented in the codebase
	b. Verify that the implementation is fully and 100% production ready with no logic gaps
	c. Verify that the implementation has no mockups, placeholders, simulations, simplifications, deffered for later, empty catch blocks, NotImplementedExceptions, Technical Debt etc.
	d. Only once the verification passes, mark it as completed.
	e. If verification fails, fix/implement it.
	f. Repeat steps from 2.a ~
3. If the task is a 'main task', 
	a. Verify that all its sub-tasks/components are marked as complete. 
	b. Only once the verification passes, mark it as completed.
	c. If verification fails, fix/implement the 'Not completed'/Partial sub-task and perform steps 2.a ~ 2.f
	d. Repeat steps from 3.a ~
----------------------------------------------------------------
Coding philosophy and architecture:
1. Microkernel + Plugins architecture
2. Kernel provides basic features, message routing and plugin load/reload/hotload. But, it is not just a plugin loaded, but a full fledged pipeline orchesterator, a post-office (message routing), and a basic storage provider (no persistance)
3. All 'Features' are provided in plugins
4. All common features/functions go into 'Ultimate' or 'Universal' plugins, only features/functions with unique requirements go to standalone plugins.
   For example, UltimateEncryption plugin handles all encryption algorithms, does everything encryption. But it doesn't handle key management - although keys are needed for encrypting and decrypting. key management is done by a separate plugin - UltimateKeyManagement which does everything related to key management. Similarly, UltimateCompression does everything related to compression, UltimateIntelligence does everything related to AI. 
5. Every plugin must implement and extend the correct type of abstract base class from the SDK.
6. SDK defines a 'Knowledge' system, where every plugin on load provides static knowledge (their features, which ones are enables, which are disabled etc.), and provide dynamic knowledge (that needs actual data reads) if and when querried.
7. This knowledge is registered into the knowledge system, which can be used by the Intelligence plugin.
8. SDK also defines a 'Capabilities' registry into which every plugin registers their capabilities. Plugins and Kernel can use the message bus to route messages and requests to other plugins based on this registry.
9. SDK also provides a socket/plug for the intelligence plugin to plug into - right in the lowest base class, so that every other base class already inherits it.
10. Base classes alerady implement common logic, life cycle etc. This reduces code duplication. plugins only have to implement their own specific feature logic.
11. Plugins and Kernels cannot directly refer to other plugins or kernel in the code. They can only directly refer the SDK. All communication should happen only through commands/messages via the message bus.
